Eleventh Proof: Allah Owns Space and Time
Imam Razi uses two Quranic verses to show Allah's ownership of space and time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses two Quranic verses to establish that Allah owns space and time, thereby demonstrating His transcendence beyond spatial and temporal dimensions.

Core Idea
Allah's ownership of space proves He is not contained by it.

Imam Razi presents the eleventh proof for divine transcendence by citing two Quranic verses: one declaring Allah's ownership of the heavens and earth (space) and the other declaring His ownership of whatever dwells in night and day (time). By showing that Allah possesses space and time, Razi argues that Allah cannot be limited by them. This lesson examines the two verses and their combined implication.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully
Start with the Arabic text and its English translation. Notice the structure: first verse, second verse, then their combination.
The passage ends abruptly, but the argument is complete enough to understand.
2
Identify the two Quranic verses and their indications
The first verse (Quran 6:12) is used to indicate that space (al-makan) belongs to Allah. The second (Quran 6:13) indicates that time (al-zaman) belongs to Him.
Razi interprets 'what is in the heavens and earth' to include space itself.
3
Understand how Razi extends ownership to space and time
Razi goes beyond the surface meaning of created objects and argues that the very containers (space and time) are owned by Allah.
This extension is key to the proof of transcendence.
4
Consider the combined implication
If Allah owns space and time, He cannot be contained by them. This reinforces His transcendence.
The combination of the two verses strengthens the argument.
5
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Many think the verses only refer to created objects, but Razi's interpretation includes the containers themselves.
This misconception is corrected by Razi's reasoning.

And the combination of the two verses indicates that space...

Commentary
This passage presents the eleventh proof from the Quran. Imam Razi quotes two verses: one declaring that everything in the heavens and earth belongs to Allah, and another declaring that whatever dwells in night and day belongs to Him. He interprets the first as indicating that 'space' (المكان) and its contents are Allah's possession, and the second as indicating that 'time' (الزمان) and its contents are also His. The combination of the two verses, Razi says, indicates something about space—presumably that space itself is owned by Allah and thus cannot contain Him. Although the passage is cut off, the argument is clear: since Allah owns space, He cannot be spatially located. This reinforces the transcendence of Allah beyond spatial dimensions.

Key Terms
مکان
زمان
ملك
آية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'what is in the heavens and earth' refers only to created objects, not to space itself.
Correction: Imam Razi explicitly extends the meaning to include space (al-makan) itself, arguing that if Allah owns all of space and time, He cannot be contained by them.

Checkpoint
What does the verse 'Say: To whom belongs what is in the heavens and the earth?' (Quran 6:12) indicate according to Imam Razi?
A) That Allah is in the heavens
B) That space belongs to Allah
C) That the heavens are eternal
D) That the earth is the center

Key Takeaway
Allah's ownership of space and time, as indicated by two Quranic verses, proves that He transcends all spatial and temporal dimensions.

Why 'Sky' Cannot Apply to Allah
Imam Razi refutes two aspects of the objection about 'sama'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Razi refutes the objection that the term 'sama' (sky) could be applied to Allah through specification, and why associating Allah with a direction is impossible.

Core Idea
Calling Allah 'sky' would make Him created – impossible.

Imam Razi addresses an objection: could the term 'sama' (sky) be applied to Allah by lexical specification? He shows that this would logically entail Allah being in a direction, which makes Him a created thing. He also explains that specification is only used in necessity, and here there is no necessity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once carefully, then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: first a conditional argument, then an objection, then two answers.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لو كان مختصاً بجهة فوق'.
2
Understand the objection
The objector claims that 'sama' can be specified to refer to Allah, since specification of general terms is allowed. Identify the two parts of the objection: customary usage and lexical origin.
3
Follow Razi's two answers
First answer: denying that 'above' applies to Allah because it would make Him a created sky. Second answer: specification is only for necessity, and no rational proof demands it.
Note the logical chain: if above → sky → created.
4
Reflect on the principle
Understand that even if a term can be specified, without rational necessity we stick to the clear proofs that negate direction from Allah.
This shows the precedence of rational proofs over lexical flexibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعالى لو كان مختصاً بجهة فوق، لكان سماء، ولو كان سماء، لكان مخلوقاً لنفسه، وهذا محال. فوجب أن لا يكون مختصاً بجهة فوق. 
فإن قيل: لفظ السماء مختص في العرف بهذه الأجرام المستديرة، وأيضاً: فهم أن هذا اللفظ في أصل الوضع يتناول ذات الله تعالى، إلا أن تخصيص العموم جائز. 
قلنا: أما الجواب عن الأول: فهو أن هذا الفوق ممنوع. وكيف لا نقول ذلك، وقد دللنا على أنه بتقدير أن يكون الله تعالى مختصاً بجهة فوق، إلا أن نسبة ذاته تعالى إلى سكان العرش كنسبة السماء إلى سكان الأرض؟ فوجب القطع بأنه لو كان مختصاً بجهة فوق لكان سماء. وأما الجواب عن الثاني: فهو أن تخصيص العموم إنما يصار إليه عند الضرورة. فلو قام دليل قاطع عقلي على كونه تعالى مختصاً بجهة فوق، لزمنا المصير إلى هذا التخصيص. وإذا لم يقم شيء من الدلائل على ذلك، بل قامت القواطع العقلية والنقلية على امتناع كونه تعالى في الجهة، لم يكن بنا إلى التزام هذا التخصيص ضرورة. فسقط هذا الكلام.
He, exalted, if He were specifically associated with a direction of above, He would be a sky, and if He were a sky, He would be a created thing for Himself, and this is impossible. So it is necessary that He not be specifically associated with a direction of above.
If it is said: The term "sky" is specifically used in common parlance for these circular bodies, and also: It is understood that this term in its original lexical sense encompasses the essence of Allah, except that specification of the general is permissible.
We say: As for the answer to the first: It is that this "above" is denied. And how can we not say that, while we have demonstrated that on the supposition that Allah is specifically associated with a direction of above, yet the relation of His essence to the inhabitants of the Throne is like the relation of the sky to the inhabitants of the earth? So it is necessary to conclude that if He were specifically associated with a direction of above, He would be a sky. And as for the answer to the second: It is that specification of the general is only resorted to in necessity. So if there were a decisive rational proof that He is specifically associated with a direction of above, we would be compelled to adopt this specification. But since there is no such proof, rather decisive rational and transmitted proofs have been established for the impossibility of His being in a direction, we have no need to commit to this specification by necessity. Thus this argument is invalidated.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. The objector claims that the term 'sama' (sky) could be applied to Allah through specification of the general. The author responds by denying the premise that Allah is in a direction above, because that would make Him a created sky. He further argues that specification is only for necessity, and here there is no necessity. The author's argument proceeds in two steps: first, logical impossibility; second, lack of proof for such specification. The passage demonstrates the method of rejecting erroneous interpretations that rely on lexical flexibility when the rational proof is clear.

Key Terms
سماء
جهة فوق
تخصيص العموم
دليل قاطع عقلي
قواطع عقلية ونقلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the term 'sama' can be applied to Allah metaphorically or by lexical specification.
Correction: The author shows that any association with direction (even lexical) implies createdness, and specification is unjustified without rational necessity.

Checkpoint
What is the main flaw the author identifies in the objector's argument about the term 'sama'?
A) The term is only used for physical bodies.
B) It would imply Allah is created.
C) Specification is never allowed.
D) The objector misquotes the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Associating Allah with direction or applying terms that imply direction is impossible because it entails createdness.

The Eleventh Proof: Possessing Place and Time
Imam Razi quotes two Quranic verses to prove Allah transcends place and time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses two Quranic verses to prove that Allah transcends place and time, and why this argument is significant.

Core Idea
Allah owns all place and time, so He cannot be contained by them.

Imam Razi presents a concise yet powerful proof for Allah's transcendence. By citing two Quranic verses that declare all things in the heavens, earth, night, and day as belonging to Allah, he draws the logical conclusion that the Creator cannot be confined by His creation. This lesson unpacks that argument and hints at a deeper wisdom in the order of the verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the English translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style and the attribution to Abu Muslim al-Isfahani.
2
Identify the two verses and their claims
The first verse is about the heavens and earth (place). The second is about night and day (time). Determine what each verse says about ownership.
The verses are from Surah al-An'am.
3
Understand the logical inference
Ask yourself: How does showing that everything in place and time is Allah's possession lead to the conclusion that He is beyond place and time? The commentary will help.
Think about the relationship between an owner and the owned.
4
Reflect on the deeper wisdom
The author mentions a 'noble secret' in the order of the verses. Consider why place is mentioned before time. The commentary offers a possible explanation.
This is an optional deeper reflection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الحادية عشر: قوله تعالى: «قل: لمن ما في السموات والأرض؟ قل: الله» مشعر بأن المكان، وكل ما فيه: ملك الله تعالى. وقوله: «وله ما سكن في الليل والنهار» يدل على أن الزمان وكل ما فيه: ملك الله تعالى. ومجموع الآيتين: يدلان على أن المكان والمكانيات، والزمان والزمانيات: كلها ملك الله تعالى. وذلك يدل على تنزيهه عن المكان والزمان. وهذا الوجه ذكره أبو مسلم الأصبهاني رحمه الله في تفسيره. واعلم أن في تقديم ذكر المكان على ذكر الزمان: سراً شريفاً، وحكمة عالية.
The eleventh proof: His statement, the Exalted: "Say: To whom belongs what is in the heavens and the earth? Say: To Allah" indicates that place, and everything in it, are the possession of Allah. And His statement: "And to Him belongs whatever rests in the night and the day" indicates that time, and everything in it, are the possession of Allah. And the combination of the two verses indicates that place and place-nouns, and time and time-nouns, are all the possession of Allah. And that indicates His transcendence over place and time. And this point was mentioned by Abu Muslim al-Isfahani, may Allah have mercy on him, in his commentary. And know that in the precedence of mentioning place over time there is a noble secret and a lofty wisdom.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents a Quranic proof for Allah's transcendence over place and time. By citing two verses that declare all things in the heavens and earth, and all things in night and day, as belonging to Allah, the author extracts the implication that since everything in place and time is His possession, He cannot be contained by them. The mention of Abu Muslim al-Isfahani shows the source. The comment about the order of mention (place before time) hints at a deeper wisdom, likely that time is dependent on motion of the spheres which exist in place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the verses only show Allah's ownership of creation, but not that He is beyond place and time.
Correction: The argument is that ownership implies the owner is not contained by the owned. Since Allah owns all places and times, He cannot be located within them.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The possession of all place and time by Allah demonstrates that He is beyond both.

The Twelfth Proof: Bearing the Throne
Imam Razi uses the verse about angels carrying the Throne to prove Allah is not on it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imām Rāzī uses the verse about angels carrying the Throne to prove that Allāh is not physically located on it, thus defending His transcendence.

Core Idea
If Allāh were on the Throne, the carriers would hold Him, making Him dependent.

Imām Rāzī now presents a proof based on a well-known Qur'anic verse about the Day of Judgment. He argues that the very act of angels carrying the Throne implies that Allāh cannot be upon it, otherwise absurd consequences follow. This lesson unpacks that logical argument and its importance for tanzīh.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source and its translation without analysis. Notice the verse and the reasoning that follows.
Focus on the logical structure: verse → conditional → absurdity.
2
Identify the key premise
The argument relies on the condition: if Allāh were on the Throne, then the bearers would be carrying Him.
3
Understand the implication
Carrying Allāh would imply He needs them, which contradicts His self-sufficiency. This is the core of the proof.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Connect to divine transcendence
Reflect on how this proof supports the doctrine that Allāh is not confined to any space or direction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية عشرة: قوله تعالى: «ويحمل عرش ربك فوقهم يومئذ: ثمانية»، ولو كان الخالق في العرش، لكان حامل العرش حاملاً لمن في العرش، فيلزم احتياج الخالق إلى المخلوق. ويقرب منه: قوله تعالى: «الذين يحملون العرش».
The twelfth proof: His statement, the Exalted: "And the Throne of your Lord will be carried above them on that Day by eight" — and if the Creator were in the Throne, then the bearer of the Throne would be carrying the One in the Throne, which would necessitate the Creator's need for the creation. And near to it is His statement: "Those who bear the Throne."
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage uses a verse about angels carrying the Throne on the Day of Judgment to prove that Allah is not on the Throne. If He were, the carriers would be carrying Him, implying He needs them, which is impossible for the Creator. The argument is straightforward and relies on the absurdity of the implication.

Key Terms

حامل العرش
احتياج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse about angels carrying the Throne only describes an event; it doesn't relate to Allah's location.
Correction: Imam Razi shows that if Allah were on the Throne, the act of carrying would imply dependence, which is impossible. So the verse indirectly proves His transcendence.

Checkpoint

A) The Throne would be too great for Him.

D) The angels would be His partners.

Key Takeaway
The verse about angels carrying the Throne implies that Allah cannot be on it, because that would necessitate His dependence on creations.

The Thirteenth Proof: Priority of Creation
Imam Razi argues from the priority of creation that Allah is not on the Throne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's logical argument that the order of creation—heavens first, then Throne—shows Allah is not established upon the Throne.

Core Idea
If the Throne were Allah's place, it would be created first—yet the heavens came first.

Imam Razi presents a logical argument based on the order of creation. If the Throne were a place for Allah, reason would require it to be created first, but the Quran states that the heavens and earth were created first, and then Allah established Himself on the Throne. This temporal priority shows the Throne is not His place.

Guided Path
1
Understand the conditional premise
Begin by examining the conditional statement: if Allah were established on the Throne, then creating the Throne would take priority over creating the heavens. Grasp the logical structure before moving on.
This is a hypothetical argument based on what would logically follow.
2
Recognize the rational axiom
The argument rests on an axiom: a sovereign's own place should be prepared before the places of his servants. This is presented as self-evident to reason.
Imam Razi assumes this rational principle is universally accepted.
3
Examine the scriptural evidence
Now look at the Quranic verse cited (7:54). Notice the word 'thumma' (then), which indicates delay. The heavens were created before the establishment on the Throne.
The verse is used as evidence for the chronological order.
4
Connect to the conclusion
Combine the rational axiom (Throne would be first if it were His place) with the scriptural evidence (heavens came first). The contradiction shows the initial assumption is false: Allah is not on the Throne.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة عشرة: لو كان تعالى مستقراً على العرش، لكان الابتداء بتخليق العرش أولى من الابتداء بتخليق السموات. لأن على تقدير القول أنه مستقر على العرش، يكون العرش مكاناً له والسموات مكان عبيده. والأقرب إلى العقول: أن تكون تهيئة مكان نفسه مقدماً على تهيئة مكان العبيد. لكن من المعلوم: أن تخليق السموات مقدم على تخليق العرش، لقوله تعالى: «إن ربكم الله الذي خلق السموات والأرض في ستة أيام، ثم استوى على العرش»، وكلمة «ثم» للتراخي.
The thirteenth proof: If the Exalted were established upon the Throne, then the beginning with creating the Throne would be more appropriate than beginning with creating the heavens. Because on the assumption that He is established on the Throne, the Throne would be a place for Him and the heavens a place for His servants. And the closest to reason is that the preparation of His own place should precede the preparation of the place of the servants. But it is known that the creation of the heavens precedes the creation of the Throne, due to His statement: "Indeed your Lord is Allah who created the heavens and the earth in six days, then He established Himself upon the Throne," and the word "thumma" indicates delay.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage presents another logical argument from the order of creation. If the Throne were Allah's place, it would be created first, as place for the sovereign. But the Quran states that the heavens and earth were created first, and then (thumma) He established on the Throne, indicating delay. Therefore, the Throne is not His place. The argument uses rational priority and textual evidence.

Key Terms
استقرار
تخليق
ثم للتراخي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'thumma' in the verse merely indicates sequence without implying priority or delay.
Correction: Imam Razi explicitly states that 'thumma' indicates delay (tardākhī), meaning the creation of the heavens occurred before the establishment on the Throne. This temporal gap is crucial for the argument.

Checkpoint
Why does the word 'thumma' (then) in the verse support the argument?
A) It shows the creation of the Throne after the heavens.
B) It shows the establishment is not literal.
C) It indicates delay, so the heavens were created before the Throne.
D) It indicates the Throne is not a place.

Key Takeaway
The priority of creation proves the Throne is not a place for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite or hear the verse 'thumma istawa 'ala al-'arsh', do you find yourself unconsciously picturing Allah 'arriving' at the Throne after creation? How can you train your mind to submit to the Qur'anic denial of spatial limits, even when your imagination rebels? Will you make a conscious effort to think of istiwa' as a divine act beyond your comprehension, rather than a physical movement?
?
This proof relies on the rational axiom that one prepares one's own place before preparing others. If the Qur'an contradicts your intuition, are you willing to abandon your mental image for the sake of true tawhid? What specific assumption about Allah will you challenge today?
?
The argument concludes that Allah is not on the Throne, yet many Muslims still talk about Allah 'above' the heavens. Does this proof unsettle you? Will you allow this logical demonstration to reshape how you speak about Allah's transcendence, even if it means correcting common phrases you've used? Commit to one change in your speech about Allah this week.

The Twelfth Proof: Throne Bearers Cannot Carry the Creator
Razi presents a Quranic argument against Allah being on the Throne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument from Quranic verses that Allah is not located on the Throne, and why this argument refutes anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
If Allah were on the Throne, the carriers would carry Him — impossible.

This lesson presents the twelfth proof from Razi's Asas al-Taqdis against the belief that Allah is physically on the Throne. Razi cites Quranic verses about the Throne being carried and draws a logical conclusion: if Allah were on it, the bearers would be carrying the Creator, implying need. He also offers a subtle insight about the priority of place over time in the verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the logical flow from verse to conclusion.
The passage includes two Quranic verses and a concluding remark.
2
Understand the logical deduction
Identify the premise: if Allah were on the Throne, then the bearers of the Throne would be carrying whoever is on it. The conclusion: that would imply the Creator needs creation, which is impossible.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Reflect on the deeper secret
Consider Razi's remark that the mention of place before time in the verse contains a noble secret. Think about how this order might point to Allah's transcendence beyond space and time.
Razi does not elaborate here, but it hints at a deeper theological insight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية عشرة : قوله تعالى: « ويحمل عرش ربك فوقهم يومئذ: ثمانية (۷۱) ، ولو كان الخالق فى العرش ، لكان حامل العرش حاملا لمن في العرش، فيلزم احتياج الخالق إلى المخلوق. ويقرب منه : قوله تعالى : الذين يحملون العرش (۷۲) ، وهذا الوجه ذكره أبو مسلم الأصبهاني (۷۰) رحمه الله في تفسيره . واعلم أن في تقديم ذكر المكان على ذكر الزمان : سراً شريفاً، وحكمة عالية.
The twelfth proof: His saying: 'And your Lord's Throne will be carried above them on that day by eight' (69:17). And if the Creator were upon the Throne, then the bearer of the Throne would be carrying whoever is upon the Throne, so the need of the Creator for the creation would follow. And near it is His saying: 'Those who bear the Throne' (40:7). And this aspect was mentioned by Abu Muslim al-Isfahani (may Allah have mercy on him) in his exegesis. And know that in the precedence of the mention of place over the mention of time there is a noble secret and a sublime wisdom.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is the twelfth proof against anthropomorphism, specifically against the idea that Allah is located on the Throne. It is a proof from the Qur'an. Razi cites two verses: first, from Surah al-Haqqa (69:17), which states that on the Day of Judgment, eight angels will carry the Throne of the Lord above the people. Second, from Surah Ghafir (40:7), which describes the angels who carry the Throne. The argument is straightforward: if Allah were actually on the Throne, then the angels carrying the Throne would also be carrying Allah. This would mean that the Creator depends on His creation for support, which is impossible. Razi then acknowledges that this point was already made by the commentator Abu Muslim al-Isfahani in his tafsir. Finally, he adds a subtle observation: in the first verse, the word 'place' (al-makan) is mentioned before 'time' (al-zaman). Razi sees this as a noble secret and sublime wisdom, implying that the priority of place over time in the verse points to the transcendence of Allah from time and space, though he does not elaborate further within this passage.

Key Terms
حامل العرش
احتياج الخالق إلى المخلوق
مكان
زمان
سر شريف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because the Throne is carried, Allah must be above it, making the Throne a literal place for Allah.
Correction: Razi shows that this belief leads to the impossible conclusion that the Creator needs creation, so Allah cannot be on the Throne.

Checkpoint
What conclusion does Razi draw from the verse about the Throne being carried?
A) The Throne is a place for Allah.
B) Allah is not on the Throne because that would imply need.
C) The angels carry Allah Himself.
D) The Throne was created before the heavens.

Key Takeaway
Razi proves that Allah cannot be on the Throne because that would make Him dependent on His creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you truly believed that Allah is not located anywhere, how would your prayer change? Would you still raise your hands as if He is above? Write down one specific change you will make this week.
?
The angels carrying the Throne are a sign of Allah's majesty. But do you sometimes feel that Allah is distant because He is beyond space? How can today's lesson renew your awe and intimacy with Him, rather than making Him seem remote?

Thirteenth Proof: Priority of Heavens Over Throne
Razi uses logical priority to deny that Allah is settled on the Throne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's logical argument that the priority of the heavens' creation over the Throne disproves the literal interpretation of Allah being settled on the Throne.

Core Idea
If the Throne were Allah's place, it should have been created before the heavens.

Razi presents his thirteenth proof against the anthropomorphic notion that Allah is literally settled on the Throne. Using simple logic and a Qur'anic verse, he shows that the order of creation contradicts this claim. This lesson walks through his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the assumption and its implications
The proof begins with a conditional: if Allah were settled on the Throne, then the Throne would be His place and the heavens the place of His servants. Recognize this initial assumption.
2
Identify the rational principle
Razi states a common-sense principle: one prepares one's own place before preparing a place for others. This principle is key to the argument.
This principle is presented as 'closer to reason'.
3
Apply the principle and check the Qur'an
If the principle holds, the Throne should have been created before the heavens. But the Qur'an (7:54) mentions creation of heavens and earth first, then 'thumma' (indicating delay) 'istawa' on the Throne. This contradicts the expectation, so the assumption is false.
The word 'thumma' is crucial; it shows the Throne's creation is later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة عشرة : لو كان تعالى مستقرا على العرش ، لكان الابتداء بتخليق العرش، أولى من الابتداء بتخليق السموات . لأن على تقدير القول أنه مستقر على العرش ، يكون العرش مكانا له والسموات مكان عبيده . والأقرب إلى العقول : أن يكون تهيئة مكان نفسه، مقدما على تهيئة مكان العييد . لكن من المعلوم : أن تخليق السموات مقدم على تخليق العرش، لقوله تعالى : ( إن ربكم الله الذي خلق السموات والأرض في ستة أيام ، ثم استوى على العرش) ، وكلمة « ثم » لتراخي .
The thirteenth proof: If the Exalted were settled on the Throne, then the beginning with the creation of the Throne would be more appropriate than the beginning with the creation of the heavens. Because on the assumption of the statement that He is settled on the Throne, the Throne would be a place for Him and the heavens a place for His servants. And the closer to reason is that preparing His own place should be prior to preparing the place of servants. But it is known that the creation of the heavens is prior to the creation of the Throne, due to His saying: 'Indeed your Lord is Allah who created the heavens and the earth in six days, then He established Himself on the Throne' (7:54). And the word 'thumma' indicates delay.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is the thirteenth proof, a logical argument against the notion that Allah is 'settled' (mustaqirr) on the Throne. Razi argues by considering what would follow if the claim were true. If Allah were settled on the Throne, the Throne would be His place, while the heavens are the place of His servants (i.e., creation). Reason dictates that one would prepare one's own place before preparing a place for others. Therefore, if the Throne were Allah's place, it should have been created before the heavens. However, the Qur'an (7:54) states that Allah created the heavens and the earth in six days, then (thumma) He established Himself on the Throne. The Arabic word 'thumma' indicates a sequence with delay, meaning the Throne was created after the heavens. Hence, the priority contradicts the assumption. Therefore, Allah is not settled on the Throne in a literal sense. The argument does not deny the verse but interprets 'istawa' differently, as is standard in Ash'ari theology.

Key Terms
مستقر على العرش
تخليق العرش
تخليق السموات
ثم للتراخي
تهيئة المكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'thumma' in the verse implies only a temporal order, not logical priority, but Razi uses it to show that the Throne was created after the heavens, contradicting the expectation if Allah were on it.
Correction: Razi's argument hinges on the sequence: the heavens were created before the Throne. If Allah were literally on the Throne, the Throne should have been created first. The verse's wording 'thumma' (then) establishes the order.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi argue that the creation of the Throne should have been before the heavens if Allah were on it?
A) Because the Throne is more important than the heavens.
B) Because one prepares one's own place before preparing a place for others.
C) Because the Throne was created first according to the Quran.
D) Because the angels carry the Throne.

Key Takeaway
The order of creation in the Qur'an contradicts the claim that Allah is literally settled on the Throne.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'then He established Himself on the Throne' in the Qur'an, have you ever subconsciously imagined Allah as sitting on a throne like a king? How does Razi's logical argument challenge that mental image? Are you willing to let go of that image even if it feels comforting?
?
Do you sometimes assume that Allah is limited by your own understanding of space and time? What would it mean for your daily worship if you truly believed that Allah is beyond all places and yet closer to you than your jugular vein?
?
If you had to explain the priority of the heavens over the Throne to someone who insists on a literal interpretation, what would you say? Would you be able to defend the transcendence of Allah with both reason and revelation, or would you rely on blind acceptance?

The Quranic Proof for Transcendence of Space
Razi cites Quran 28:88 and deduces Allah's transcendence of space.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's use of the Quranic verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face' to argue that Allah is transcendent of space, and the initial objection that spaces are not real things.

Core Idea
The Quran proves Allah's transcendence through annihilation of all spaces.

Razi presents the fourteenth proof for Allah's transcendence of space, based on the Quranic verse (28:88). He argues that since everything will perish, including the Throne and all spaces, Allah will remain without space. This implies He is not in a place now. An immediate objection arises: spaces are not existing things, so how can they perish? This lesson covers the initial proof and the objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and Razi's interpretation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Razi interprets the verse to include the Throne and all spaces.
The verse appears to be general, covering everything.
2
Understand the logical move
Razi argues from the future state (after annihilation) to the present: if Allah will exist without space later, He must be without space now, otherwise change would occur.
This is a key step in the argument.
3
Identify the objection
The objection claims that spaces and directions are not real entities, so they cannot be said to perish.
This objection sets up the next lesson's response.
4
Reflect on why this matters
Ask yourself: If spaces are not real, does the verse still prove Allah is not in a place? How would Razi answer?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة عشرة : قوله تعالى : كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه .. ظاهر الآية يقتضى فناء العرش ، وفناء جميع الأحياز والجهات . وحينئذ يبقى الحق سبحانه وتعالى منزها عن الحيز والجهة . وإذا ثبت ذلك، امتنع أن يكون الآن فى جهة ( وحيز ) وإلا لزم وقوع التغير في الذات. فإن قيل : الحيز والجهة ليس شيئا موجودا ، حتى يصير هالكا فانيا . قلنا : الأحياز و الجهات أمور متخالفة بحقائقها ، متباينة بماهياتها ، بدليل : أنكم قلتم : إنه يجب حصول ذات الله تعالى في جهة فوق ، ويمتنع حصول ذاته فى سائر الجهات . فلولا أن جهة فوق مخالفة بالماهية لسائر الجهات ( وإلا ) لما كانت جهة فوق مخالفة لسائر الجهات في هذه الخاصة ، وهذا الحكم. وأيضا : فإنا نقول : هذا الجسم حصل في هذا الحيز ، بعد أن كان حاصلا فى حيز آخر . فهذه الأحياز معدودة متباينة متعاقبة، والعدم المحض لا يكون كذلك. فثبت : أن هذه الأحياز أمور متخالفة بالحقائق ، متباينة بالعدد . وكل ما كان كذلك ، امتنع أن يكون عدما محضا . فكان أمرا موجودا . وإذا ثبت هذا ، دخل تحت قوله تعالى : كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه ، وإذا هلك الحيز والجهة ، بقى ذات الله تعالى منزها عن الحيز والجهة وبقية الكلام قد تقدمت .
The fourteenth proof: His saying: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' (28:88). The apparent meaning of the verse necessitates the annihilation of the Throne and the annihilation of all spaces and directions. Then the Truth, exalted and high, remains transcendent of space and direction. And if this is established, it is impossible that He is now in a direction and space, otherwise change would occur in the Essence. If it is said: 'Space and direction are not an existing thing, so that they become perished and annihilated.' We say: Spaces and directions are things differing in their realities, distinct in their quiddities, as evidence: that you said it is necessary for the Essence of Allah to be in a direction of above and impossible for His Essence to be in other directions. For were it not that the direction of above differs in quiddity from other directions, then the direction of above would not differ from other directions in this specific property and this ruling. Also, we say: This body came to be in this space after having been in another space. So these spaces are enumerated, distinct, successive, and pure nothingness is not like that. So it is established that these spaces are things differing in realities, distinct in number. And everything that is like that is impossible to be pure nothingness. So it is an existing thing. And when this is established, it falls under His saying: 'Everything is perishing except His Face.' And when space and direction perish, the Essence of Allah remains transcendent of space and direction. And the rest of the discussion has preceded.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is the fourteenth proof, a Quranic and rational argument for Allah's transcendence of space and direction. Razi begins with the verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face' (Q. 28:88). He observes that the plain meaning of the verse implies that the Throne, and also all spaces (ahiyaz) and directions (jihaat), will perish, since they are included in 'everything'. After they perish, only Allah remains. Therefore, since Allah will exist without space and direction after the annihilation, He must be free of them now as well; otherwise, His nature would change (which is impossible for the divine essence). Razi then considers a likely objection: spaces and directions are not real things (they are nothing), so they cannot be 'perishing'. He refutes this in two ways. First, he uses the opponent's own admission: the claim that Allah exists in the direction 'above' but not in other directions implies that these directions have distinct quiddities (māhiyāt). If they were identical, there would be no reason for one direction to be for Allah and others not. Thus, directions are real and distinct. Second, he argues from physical bodies: a body moves from one space to another, so spaces are countable, distinct, and successive. Pure nothingness cannot have such properties. Therefore, spaces are existing things. Consequently, they fall under the verse's generalization that everything (including them) will perish. Hence, after their perishing, Allah remains without space, proving He is not in a place now. Razi ends by noting that the rest of the discussion has been presented earlier (referring to previous arguments).

Key Terms
كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه
الحيز
الجهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Spaces and directions are just empty nothingness, not existing entities.
Correction: Razi will later argue that spaces are real because they have distinct quiddities and are countable, so they fall under the verse's generality.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's interpretation, what will perish according to the verse?
A) Only the Throne
B) Everything except Allah's Face
C) Only humans
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face' implies that Allah will exist without space after annihilation, so He must be free of space now.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If everything in your life—your home, your mosque, your city, the entire universe—will one day perish completely, where is your ultimate security? Do you truly anchor your heart in Allah alone, or are you secretly reliant on some 'space' that feels permanent?
?
The verse declares that only Allah's 'Face' remains. What does it mean for you to seek His Face in your daily actions? Are there any actions you do where you are seeking something other than His pleasure?
?
Allah is not confined to any place—not even the heavens. When you pray, do you sometimes imagine Allah as 'up there'? How does this lesson challenge that assumption, and how can you adjust your awareness of His presence to be truly without location?

Refuting the Objection: Spaces Are Real
Razi refutes the objection that spaces are unreal with two proofs and concludes the argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's two proofs that spaces and directions are real existing things, and how this supports the argument for Allah's transcendence of space.

Core Idea
Spaces are real and distinct; therefore they perish, proving Allah is beyond space.

Razi now responds to the objection that spaces are not real. He offers two arguments: first, based on the opponent's own claim that Allah is in a specific direction ('above'), which implies directions have distinct quiddities. Second, based on the fact that bodies move between spaces, showing spaces are countable and distinct. These proofs establish that spaces are existing things, and thus they fall under the verse's generality, leading to the conclusion that Allah remains transcendent of space.

Guided Path
1
Read Razi's response
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Note the structure: objection, then two proofs, then conclusion.
2
Understand the first proof
Razi uses the opponent's own belief that Allah is in a specific direction ('above') to argue that directions have distinct quiddities (essences). If they were identical, there would be no reason for Allah to be in one and not another.
This shows directions are real and distinct.
3
Understand the second proof
Razi points out that bodies move from one space to another; spaces are countable, distinct, and successive. Pure nothingness cannot have these properties, so spaces must be existing things.
This argument uses physical observation.
4
Follow the conclusion
Since spaces are real, they are included in the verse's 'everything'. Thus, when they perish, Allah remains without space, confirming His transcendence.
The argument is complete.

Fourteenth Proof: Annihilation of Space from Quran 28:88
Razi argues from the annihilation of all things except Allah's Face that Allah is free of space.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi uses Quran 28:88 to prove that Allah is free of space and direction, and why spaces and directions are considered real existing things that perish.

Core Idea
Everything except Allah perishes — including space itself.

Imam al-Razi presents a profound Quranic argument for Allah's transcendence. The verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face' (28:88) seems straightforward, but al-Razi unpacks its implications for the nature of space and direction. He anticipates an objection: aren't spaces just nothing? His answer demonstrates that they are real, created entities, and thus subject to annihilation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse and al-Razi's inference
Read the verse and notice how al-Razi infers that the Throne, spaces, and directions are included in 'everything' and thus perish. Then see how he concludes that Allah remains transcendent.
The verse is from Surah al-Qasas 28:88.
2
Understand the objection
The objection claims that space and direction are not 'things' (ashya') that can perish. Pause to consider why someone might think this.
3
Follow al-Razi's two-part refutation
Al-Razi gives two arguments: 1) Different directions have distinct quiddities (e.g., 'above' is not the same as 'below'), so they are real. 2) Bodies move between spaces, showing spaces are distinct and successive, unlike non-existence.
This establishes that spaces are existing things.
4
See how the proof completes
Since spaces are real, they fall under the verse's generality and perish. Thus Allah remains, proving He is not in a direction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة عشرة : قوله تعالى : كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه (۷۰) .. ظاهر الآية يقتضى فناء العرش ، وفناء جميع الأحياز والجهات . وحينئذ يبقى الحق سبحانه وتعالى منزها عن الحيز والجهة . وإذا ثبت ذلك، امتنع أن يكون الآن فى جهة ( وحيز ) (٧٦) وإلا لزم وقوع التغير في الذات. فإن قيل : الحيز والجهة ليس شيئا موجودا ، حتى يصير هالكا فانيا . قلنا : الأحياز و الجهات أمور متخالفة (۷۷) بحقائقها ، متباينة بماهياتها ، بدليل : أنكم قلتم : إنه يجب حصول ذات الله تعالى في جهة فوق ، ويمتنع حصول ذاته فى سائر الجهات . فلولا أن جهة فوق مخالفة بالماهية لسائر الجهات ( وإلا ) (۷۸) لما كانت جهة فوق مخالفة لسائر الجهات في هذه الخاصة ، وهذا الحكم. وأيضا : فلانا نقول : هذا الجسم حصل في هذا الحيز ، بعد أن كان حاصلا فى حيز آخر . فهذه الأحياز معدودة متباينة متعاقبة، والعدم المحض لا يكون كذلك. فثبت : أن هذه الأحياز أمور متخالفة بالحقائق ، متباينة بالعدد . وكل ما كان كذلك ، امتنع أن يكون عدما محضا . فكان أمرا موجودا . وإذا ثبت هذا ، دخل تحت قوله تعالى : كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه (۷۹) ، وإذا هلك الحيز والجهة ، بقى ذات الله تعالى منزها عن الحيز والجهة (۸۰) وبقية الكلام قد تقدمت .
The fourteenth proof: His statement, the Most High: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' (28:88). The apparent meaning of the verse necessitates the annihilation of the Throne, and the annihilation of all spaces and directions. Then the Truth, glorified and exalted, remains transcendent of space and direction. If that is established, it is impossible that He be now in a direction and a space, otherwise change in the Essence would follow. If it is said: 'Space and direction are not an existing thing such that they become perishing and annihilated.' We say: Spaces and directions are things differing in their realities, distinct in their quiddities, by evidence: that you have said that it is necessary for the Essence of Allah the Most High to be in the direction of above, and it is impossible for His Essence to be in other directions. Were it not that the direction of above differs in quiddity from other directions, then the direction of above would not differ from other directions in this particularity and this ruling. And also: we say: This body came to be in this space after it had come to be in another space. These spaces are enumerated, distinct, successive, and absolute non-existence is not like that. So it is established that these spaces are things differing in realities, distinct in number. Everything that is like that is impossible to be absolute non-existence. So it was an existing thing. If this is established, it falls under His statement, the Most High: 'Everything is perishing except His Face.' When space and direction perish, the Essence of Allah the Most High remains transcendent of space and direction. The rest of the discourse has preceded.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents the fourteenth proof from the Quran for Allah's transcendence (tanzih) of space and direction. The proof is a definition-and-argument passage: Razi defines the import of ayat al-kursi? No, it's from Surah al-Qasas 28:88. The argument is: The verse says everything perishes except Allah's Face. This includes the Throne, and by implication all spaces and directions. If spaces and directions are among 'everything', they must perish. After they perish, Allah remains, so He is not dependent on space or direction. If He were in a direction now, He would change after its annihilation. Then Razi anticipates an objection: spaces and directions are not 'things' (ashya') to be subject to annihilation. He answers by proving they are existing things. First, Muslims affirm that Allah is above (direction of 'above') and not in other directions, showing that directions have distinct quiddities. Second, bodies move between spaces, proving spaces are distinct, successive, and thus not pure non-existence. Therefore spaces are real existing things that fall under the verse's generality. Thus the proof stands: space and direction perish, and Allah remains transcendent.

Key Terms
حيز
جهة
هالك
وجه الله
ماهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Spaces and directions are mere nothing (non-existence) and do not need to be considered as created things.
Correction: Razi proves that spaces and directions have distinct quiddities and are countable, so they are real existing entities that are subject to annihilation.

Checkpoint
According to the fourteenth proof, why does the verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face' entail that Allah is not in a spatial direction?
A) Because the Throne is the greatest direction, and it perishes.
B) Because all spaces and directions are included in 'everything', so they perish; if Allah were in one, He would change.
C) Because Allah's Face is a spatial direction that remains.
D) Because the verse only applies to bodies, not to Allah.

Key Takeaway
The annihilation of all things includes space and direction, proving that Allah is utterly transcendent and not confined to any place.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray, do you find yourself instinctively 'pointing' your heart to a direction in the sky? How would your prayer change if you truly internalized that Allah is beyond all directions?
?
This proof says that even 'space' is an existing thing that perishes. What does that imply about the permanence of anything you rely on except Allah? Is there a 'space' in your life—a relationship, a role, a possession—that you treat as if it will never vanish?
?
Razi uses the fact that directions differ in quiddity to prove their reality. In what ways do you define your own identity by 'directions'—such as social status, affiliations, or physical location? If all those distinctions are created and doomed to perish, who are you without them?

Fifteenth Proof: Divine Priority and Posteriority
Razi presents a Quranic proof for Allah's independence from space and direction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the Quranic verse 'He is the First and the Last' to prove that Allah is transcendent over space and direction.

Core Idea
Allah's being 'First and Last' means He precedes and outlasts all creation, including space itself.

In this proof, Imam Razi turns to a well-known Quranic verse that ascribes to Allah the attributes of 'the First' and 'the Last'. These two names are often understood in a temporal sense, but Razi shows they have a deeper implication: they entail that Allah's existence is prior to everything other than Him, including the very dimensions of space and direction. By establishing that Allah was before space and will remain after space is gone, Razi demonstrates that Allah is not confined by location.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Notice the concise style of Razi's argument.
2
Follow the logical chain
Identify the inference: from the verse 'He is the First and the Last' to priority/posteriority to everything, then to existence before and after space.
The phrase 'كل ما سواه' (everything other than Him) is key—it includes space.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why this proof refutes anthropomorphism: if Allah exists before and after space, He cannot be located within it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة عشرة : قوله تعالى : ( هو الأول والآخر (۸۱) ، فهو يقتضى أن يكون ذاته متقدما في الوجود على كل ما سواه ، وأن يكون متأخرا في الوجود عن كل ما سواه ، وذلك يقتضى أنه كان موجودا قبل الحيز والجهة ، ويكون موجودا بعد فناء الحيز والجهة . وإذا ثبت هذا، فالتقريب ما ذكرناه في الحجة الثالثة عشرة ، والرابعة عشرة .
The fifteenth proof: His statement, the Most High: 'He is the First and the Last' (57:3). So it requires that His Essence be prior in existence to everything other than Him, and that He be posterior in existence to everything other than Him. And that requires that He existed before space and direction, and that He exists after the annihilation of space and direction. If this is established, then the approach is what we mentioned in the thirteenth and fourteenth proofs.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the Quranic attribute 'He is the First and the Last' (al-Awwal wa al-Akhir). Razi explains that these attributes imply that Allah's Essence is prior to all created existence and also posterior to all created existence. Since space and direction are created things, they are included in 'everything other than Him'. Therefore, Allah existed before space and direction and will exist after they are annihilated. This entails that He is not dependent on space or direction. Razi then refers back to the earlier proofs (thirteenth and fourteenth) for the fuller elaboration of how this implies transcendence.

Key Terms
الأول (the First)
الآخر (the Last)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'First and Last' only refer to time, implying Allah is inside time.
Correction: Razi extends the meaning to include all creation, especially space and direction. Allah is before and after space, not just time.

Checkpoint

A) It requires that Allah is present in all spaces.
B) It requires that Allah existed before space and will exist after it.
C) It requires that space is part of Allah's essence.
D) It requires that Allah is limited by space.

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes 'the First' and 'the Last' prove His transcendence over space and direction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What does it mean for your daily worries to know that Allah (al-Awwal) existed before every problem you face, and al-Akhir will remain after every trial ends? How can this truth reshape your sense of urgency or anxiety today?
?
If Allah is independent of space and direction, then no place can contain Him and no direction limits Him. Where do you seek comfort or security—in places, people, or in the One who is beyond all that? What practical step can you take this week to redirect your reliance from creation to the Creator?
?
Razi argues that being 'First and Last' implies Allah is before and after 'everything other than Him', including space itself. Does your heart truly accept that Allah is closer to you than your own jugular vein (Qaf 50:16) even though He is not located anywhere? How would your prayer change if you remembered that you are not speaking into empty space but to the One who precedes and outlasts all existence?

Prostration and Nearness: A Logical Proof
Razi presents a logical proof from Quran 96:19 that Allah is not in a spatial direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses the command to prostrate and draw near to argue that Allah is not spatially located above.

Core Idea
Prostration implies nearness; if Allah were above, prostration would increase distance.

Imam Razi continues his series of Qur'anic proofs for divine transcendence. This proof is remarkably concise: it takes a single verse and extracts a logical contradiction in the anthropomorphic view. Let's examine how the command to prostrate and draw near undermines the notion that Allah is physically above.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how Razi cites the verse and immediately applies logical reasoning.
The verse is from Surah al-Alaq (96:19).
2
Identify the key terms
The argument hinges on four terms: prostration (sajdah), nearness (qurb), distance (bu'd), and direction of above (jihat al-fawq). Understand their meanings in this context.
These terms form the logical pivot of the proof.
3
Unpack the conditional reasoning
Razi uses an 'if...then' structure: if Allah were in the direction of above, then prostration would indicate distance, not nearness. Trace this logic step by step.
Consider why lowering oneself would be moving away from a being that is above.
4
Connect to the principle
Razi concludes by stating that this outcome is 'contrary to the principle' (khilaf al-asl). The principle is that worship, especially prostration, brings one closer to Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة عشرة : قوله تعالى : « واسجد واقترب (۸۲) ، ولو كان فى جهة الفوق ، لكانت السجدة تفيد البعد من الله تعالى ، لا القرب منه . وذلك خلاف الأصل
The sixteenth proof: His statement, the Most High: 'And prostrate and draw near' (96:19). And if He were in the direction of above, the prostration would indicate distance from Allah the Most High, not nearness to Him. That is contrary to the principle.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a concise proof from the Quranic command to prostrate and draw near (Surah al-Alaq 96:19). Razi argues that if Allah were spatially above, then when a person prostrates (lowering their head to the ground), they would be moving away from Allah, not drawing nearer. Since the verse explicitly links prostration with drawing near (qurb), this contradicts the assumption that Allah is in a physical direction. The 'principle' (asl) is that worship brings nearness to Allah; but if He were spatially above, prostration would produce spatial distance, not spiritual nearness.

Key Terms
سجدة (prostration)
قرب (nearness)
بعد (distance)
جهة الفوق (direction of above)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prostration is merely a physical posture with no logical implications about Allah's location.
Correction: Razi shows that the very act of prostration, when combined with the verse's promise of nearness, logically precludes Allah being spatially above.

Checkpoint
According to the sixteenth proof, what logical problem arises if Allah is in the direction of above?
A) Prostration would be impossible because the ground is below.
B) Prostration would move the worshipper away from Allah, contrary to 'draw near'.
C) The verse only applies to angels, not humans.
D) Prostration is only for idols, not Allah.

Key Takeaway
Razi's sixteenth proof demonstrates that the Qur'anic command to prostrate and draw near logically entails that Allah is not physically above, because prostration would otherwise produce distance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself imagining Allah as being 'up there' in a physical sense? After this lesson, how will you correct that image in your mind, and what does it mean for your worship to truly believe He is not limited by direction?
?
When you prostrate in prayer, do you feel closer to Allah? This lesson says the act itself signifies nearness. If you don't feel that, what might be missing in your prostration? Commit to one change in your sujood this week.
?
The proof shows that even a simple physical action carries theological weight. Are you careful to reflect on the meanings of your worship acts, or are they empty routines? What other rituals might reveal deeper truths about Allah if you pondered them?

Seventeenth Proof: Quran 2:22 on Making Equals to Allah
Razi argues from Quran 2:22 that attributing a body to Allah implies having an equal, contradicting the prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic prohibition of making equals to Allah (2:22) refutes the view that Allah is a body, because all bodies are essentially similar.

Core Idea
If Allah were a body, He would have an equal—contradicting the Quran.

This lesson examines Imam Razi's seventeenth proof for divine transcendence, drawn from Quran 2:22. The verse prohibits making 'andad' (equals) to Allah. Razi argues that if Allah were a body, He would be like all other bodies, thus creating an equal—a direct violation of the command. This proof highlights the necessary implication of corporeality: similarity and multiplicity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the literal translation to grasp the flow of Razi's argument.
Notice the key term 'nidd' (equal) and its significance.
2
Understand the term 'nidd'
Razi defines 'nidd' as a likeness of equal. This is central to the proof. The verse forbids making any equal to Allah.
Consider why a body would necessarily be an equal to other bodies.
3
Trace the logical chain
Follow the argument: (1) Quran prohibits equals. (2) If Allah were a body, He would be similar to all bodies. (3) Thus, He would have an equal. (4) This contradicts the verse.
Razi promises to prove later that all bodies are similar—this is a key premise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة عشرة : قوله تعالى : « فلا تجعلوا الله أندادا وأنتم تعلمون (۸۳) والند : المثل . ولو كان تعالى جسما لكان مثلا لكل واحد من الأجسام . لما سنبين إن شاء الله تعالى : أن الأجسام كلها متماثلة . وحينئذ يكون الند موجودا على هذا التقدير . وذلك على مضادة هذا النص .
The seventeenth proof: His statement, the Most High: 'So do not make equals to Allah while you know' (2:22). And 'al-nidd' is the likeness. And if He, the Most High, were a body, He would be a likeness to each one of the bodies, because we will explain, Allah willing, that all bodies are similar. Then on this supposition, an equal would exist. And that is contrary to this text.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from Quran 2:22, which forbids making 'andad' (equals) to Allah. The word 'nidd' means a likeness or equal. Razi argues that if Allah were a body (jism), then He would be a likeness to every other body, because (as he will later prove) all bodies are similar in their essential nature (mutamathila). If all bodies are similar, then any body would be an 'nidd' to another. Therefore, if Allah were a body, He would have an equal, which directly contradicts the prohibition. The argument relies on the premise of the similarity of all bodies, which Razi promises to prove later.

Key Terms
ند (equal/likeness)
جسم (body)
متماثلة (similar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'body' is a neutral term, and that Allah could be a body without implying anything about equals.
Correction: Razi shows that calling Allah a body necessarily implies similarity to other bodies, which leads to having an equal—contradicting the Quranic prohibition.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi argue that if Allah were a body, He would have an 'equal' (nidd) according to the seventeenth proof?
A) Because all bodies are made of matter.
B) Because all bodies are essentially similar, so any body would be a likeness to another.
C) Because the verse forbids worshiping any body.
D) Because the Quran says Allah is a body.

Key Takeaway
Razi's seventeenth proof shows that attributing a body to Allah would necessitate an equal, contradicting the Quranic command.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself imagining Allah in a certain form or shape, even if only in your subconscious? How does this verse (2:22) and Razi's proof confront your heart? Will you actively train your mind to think of Allah as beyond all physical attributes, starting today?
?
Consider the things in your life that you may be unconsciously equating with Allah—status, wealth, relationships, or even your own intellect. How does the prohibition of making 'andad' challenge you to reorder your priorities and worship?
?
Razi argues that any body is similar to another body. If you truly believe Allah is incomparable, why do you sometimes compare His power or attributes to that of created beings? Commit to reading this proof whenever such thoughts arise, and ask Allah to purify your tawhid.

The Eighteenth Proof: Hadith of Divine Pre-existence
Razi cites the hadith and draws a logical conclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith 'Allah was, and there was nothing with Him' negates any coexisting space or direction.

Core Idea
The hadith of Imran ibn Husayn proves Allah's absolute transcendence of space.

Imam Razi draws on a well-known hadith to reinforce the doctrine of divine transcendence. The Prophet's statement that Allah was alone with nothing else provides a powerful refutation of those who claim Allah occupies a space or direction. This lesson unpacks the logic of this proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its context
Read the Arabic text and translation. Notice that the Prophet's response is about 'the beginning of this matter', which Razi interprets as pre-existence.
The hadith is narrated by Imran ibn Husayn.
2
Identify Razi's logical deduction
Razi argues that if Allah were in a space, that space would be something existing with Him, contradicting 'nothing was with Him'. Follow this reasoning step by step.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this hadith settles the question of direction and place for Allah. Ask yourself: what would it mean if Allah were in a space? How does the hadith rule that out?
This connects to the broader theme of divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة عشرة : الحديث المشهور : وهو ما روى أن عمران بن الحصين قال : يا رسول الله أخبرنا عن أول هذا الأمر . فقال : كان الله ، ولم يكن معه شيء ، وقد دللنا مرارا كثيرة على أنه تعالى لو كان مختصا بالحيز والجهة ، لكان ذلك الحيز شيئا موجودا معه . وذلك على نقيض هذا النص
The eighteenth proof: The well-known hadith, and it is what is narrated that Imran ibn Husayn said: O Messenger of Allah, inform us about the beginning of this matter. He said: 'Allah was, and there was nothing with Him.' And we have demonstrated many times that if He, the Most High, were particularized by a space and a direction, that space would be a thing existing with Him. That is contrary to this text.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a proof from a well-known hadith narrated by Imran ibn Husayn. The Prophet said: 'Allah was, and there was nothing with Him.' Razi argues that if Allah were in a specific space or direction, that space would be something existing together with Him, contradicting the hadith's statement that nothing was with Him. The hadith establishes absolute divine solitude in pre-existence, which negates any coexisting space or direction. Razi notes that this argument has been demonstrated repeatedly.

Key Terms
كان الله ولم يكن معه شيء (Allah was and nothing was with Him)
حيز (space)
جهة (direction)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might interpret the hadith as only denying creation (i.e., nothing was created with Him), but not denying other entities like space.
Correction: Razi shows that the hadith says 'nothing was with Him' which includes any existing thing, including space. If space existed with Allah, it would be a thing alongside Him, contradicting the hadith.

Checkpoint
How does the hadith 'Allah was, and there was nothing with Him' negate Allah being in a space?
A) Because space is created later, not pre-existing.
B) Because if He were in a space, that space would be something with Him, contradicting 'nothing with Him'.
C) Because the hadith only applies to the beginning of creation.
D) Because space is not a 'thing'.

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'Allah was, and there was nothing with Him' conclusively proves that Allah is not confined to any space or direction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet's words 'Allah was, and there was nothing with Him' leave no room for anything beside Allah. Is there anything in your life that you have mentally placed alongside Allah as if it existed with Him? What would it take to remove that false companion?
?
If Allah is not confined to any space, then He is present to you everywhere. Do you live with the awareness of His constant presence, or do you only feel Him in specific places like the mosque? What needs to change about your daily awareness of Allah?
?
The hadith informs us about the beginning. But does it change how you think about the present? Are you living as if Allah were limited by time or place? How can you adjust your daily actions to reflect His transcendence and sovereignty over all existence?

The Hadith on 'Ama' and Negation of Direction
Razi examines a hadith to negate direction from Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith about 'ama' is interpreted to negate spatial direction from Allah, and why the reading with qasr (blindness) is preferred.

Core Idea
The hadith of 'ama' shows Allah was before creation with no location.

Imam Razi introduces the nineteenth proof, a hadith where the Prophet was asked about Allah's location before creation. The answer 'in 'ama' has been understood in two ways: as 'thin cloud' or as 'blindness'. Razi reports that scholars prefer the latter reading because it negates any direction or place, supporting the doctrine of tanzih (transcendence). In this lesson, we will examine the hadith and its interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its variants
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice that the word 'ama' can be read with madd or qasr, and each has a different meaning.
The hadith is about Allah's existence before creation.
2
Understand the two interpretations
The word 'ama' with madd means thin cloud; with qasr means blindness. Identify which interpretation supports negation of direction.
3
See the conclusion from qasr
The qasr reading indicates a state opposite to sight, metaphorically meaning no spatial context, thus negating any direction for Allah.
This is key to the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة عشرة : روى أن النبي ما قيل له : أين كان ربنا ؟ قال كان في عماء ليس تحته ماء ، ولا فوقه هواء ، قيل : العماء - بالمد - : : الغيم الرقيق. وأما العمى بالقصر - : فهو عبارة عن الحالة المضادة للبصر . وقال بعض العلماء : يجب أن تكون الرواية الصحيحة هي الرواية بالقصر لأنها تدل على نفى الجهة . لأن الجهة إذا لم تكن موجودة ، لم تكن
The nineteenth proof: It is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ was asked: 'Where was our Lord?' He said: 'He was in 'ama' – there is no water beneath it, nor air above it.' It was said: 'Al-'ama' (with madd) is the thin cloud. As for 'al-'ama' with qasr, it is an expression for the state opposite to sight.' And some scholars said: The correct narration should be the one with qasr, because it indicates negation of direction. Because when direction does not exist, it is not...
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a proof from a hadith where the Prophet was asked about the location of Allah before creation. The answer was 'He was in 'ama' – neither water below nor air above.' The word 'ama' can be read with madd (al-'ama', meaning thin cloud) or with qasr (al-'ama, meaning blindness). Razi reports that some scholars prefer the qasr reading, because it indicates a state that negates any spatial direction. The argument is incomplete in this window, but the intention is clear: the word 'ama' (with qasr) means a state of 'blindness' or absence of perception, which metaphorically indicates that there was no location or direction, thus Allah was not in any place. The phrase 'because when direction does not exist' is cut off, but presumably continues to show that if there is no direction, Allah cannot be in one.

Key Terms
عماء (with madd: cloud)
عمى (with qasr: blindness)
جهة (direction)
أين (where)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith suggests Allah was in a physical cloud (amā).
Correction: The qasr reading indicates 'blindness', meaning no spatial direction, confirming Allah's transcendence.

Checkpoint
Why do some scholars prefer the reading 'al-'ama' with qasr (blindness) in the hadith about where our Lord was?
A) Because it is more grammatically correct.
B) Because it indicates a state that negates spatial direction.
C) Because it refers to a specific cloud where Allah resides.
D) Because it is the only reading found in early manuscripts.

Key Takeaway
The hadith about 'ama' is interpreted to negate any spatial direction from Allah, supporting the doctrine of tanzih.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine Allah, do you subconsciously picture Him as 'somewhere'—perhaps above the sky? How does this hadith challenge that image, and what does it mean for your worship?
?
If Allah is beyond all directions, then He is equally close to every place. Does this truth make you more mindful of His presence, or do you find it hard to connect without a sense of physical nearness?
?
The Prophet's answer to 'where was our Lord?' points to a reality before creation. How does reflecting on Allah's existence without any location change the way you think about His eternity and your own dependence on Him?

Proof from Quran 96:19: Prostration Implies Nearness
Razi argues that prostration brings nearness, so God is not in a direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses Quran 96:19 to argue that God is not located in any spatial direction.

Core Idea
Prostration brings nearness, not distance – so God cannot be above.

Imam Razi presents the sixteenth proof for divine transcendence, drawing from the Quranic command to prostrate and draw near. He argues that if God were physically above, bowing would move the worshiper away, contradicting the verse. This lesson unpacks that concise but powerful argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Razi directly quotes the Quran and then draws a logical conclusion.
The verse is from Surah al-Alaq, verse 19.
2
Understand the logical structure
Razi uses a conditional argument: if God were in the direction of above, then prostration would imply distance, not nearness. But the verse states the opposite, so the premise must be false.
This is a proof by contradiction.
3
Reflect on the implication for divine transcendence
Think about why this argument supports the idea that God is beyond all spatial directions. How does it reinforce tanzih?
This connects to the broader theme of divine transcendence.

الحجة السادسة عشرة : قوله تعالى : « واسجد واقترب (۸۲) ، ولو كان فى جهة الفوق ، لكانت السجدة تفيد البعد من الله تعالى ، لا القرب منه . وذلك خلاف الأصل

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the Quran (Surah al-Alaq, verse 19). Razi argues that if God were located in a spatial direction such as 'above,' then performing prostration—which lowers the head—would actually move the worshiper away from God, contradicting the verse's explicit statement that prostration draws one nearer. Therefore, God cannot be in any direction, and the verse supports divine transcendence (tanzih) beyond spatial location.

Quranic Proof Against Rival Gods
Razi presents the seventeenth proof from Quran 2:22 against divine corporeality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses Quran 2:22 to argue that God cannot be a body, because it would imply a rival (nidd) which the verse forbids.

Core Idea
If God were a body, He would be like all other bodies, making a rival — which the Quran prohibits.

Razi presents a concise proof from the Quran to defend divine transcendence. The verse 'So do not attribute to Allah equals' is used to show that if God were a body, He would necessarily be an equal to every other body. This would contradict the clear command of the text. Let's examine the logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof passage
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the definition of 'nidd'.
2
Understand the key term 'nidd'
Razi defines 'nidd' as 'al-mithl' (likeness). This is crucial for the argument.
3
Grasp the premise of body similarity
Razi states that all bodies are similar (mutamathila), a premise he will prove later.
This premise is essential to the conclusion.
4
See the conclusion
If God were a body, He would be like each body, thus a nidd would exist, contrary to the Quran.
5
Reflect on the implication
The proof defends tawhid and God's transcendence from being a body.
Consider how this argument fits into broader kalam discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة عشرة : قوله تعالى : « فلا تجعلوا الله أندادا وأنتم تعلمون (۸۳) والند : المثل . ولو كان تعالى جسمها لكان مثلا لكل واحد من الأجسام . لما سنبين إن شاء الله تعالى : أن الأجسام كلها متماثلة . وحينئذ يكون الند موجودا على هذا التقدير . وذلك على مضادة هذا النص
The seventeenth proof: His saying, exalted: 'So do not attribute to Allah equals while you know' (83). And al-nidd (equal) means the likeness. And if He, exalted, were a body, He would be a likeness to each one of the bodies—since we will explain, if Allah wills, that all bodies are similar (mutamathila). Then the equal would exist on this supposition. And that is contrary to this text.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the Quran (Surah al-Baqarah, verse 22). Razi argues that God prohibits setting up equals (andad, sing. nidd). He defines nidd as 'the likeness' (al-mithl). He then states a premise to be proven later: all bodies are similar (mutamathila) in their essential nature. Therefore, if God were a body, He would be similar to every other body, and thus a 'nidd' would exist. But the Quran forbids that, so God cannot be a body.

Key Terms

متماثلة

Misconception: If God were a body, He would be unique among bodies.
Correction: Razi asserts that all bodies are similar (mutamathila) in their essential nature, so any body would be like another, creating a rival (nidd).
